## Contexts in which the word **votes** was used in the House of Representatives during the 1970s

* What was the number of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in (a) each State and (b) Australia in each of the past five elections for (i) the House of Representatives and (ii) the Senate? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700319_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-51-13)

* What was the percentage of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in each case? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700319_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-51-13)

* Has a check been made in any electoral division to ascertain what percentage of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> which Divisional Returning Officers were satisfied had been recorded prior to the close of the poll on 25th October 1969 were posted in envelopes stamped after the close of the poll. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700414_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-36-6)

* If so, what divisions and how many <span class="highlight">votes</span> were involved. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700414_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-36-6)

* What percentages of <span class="highlight">votes</span> at the House of Representatives election on 25 October 1969 were (a) ordinary, (b) postal and (c) absent <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700414_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-36-4)

* What percentages of <span class="highlight">votes</span> for candidates whose names were placed first on the ballot papers at that election were (a) ordinary, (b) postal and (c) absent <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700414_reps_27_hor66/#subdebate-36-4)

* If it was not for the Government's fear of losing <span class="highlight">votes</span> from that kind of result, this would be the appropriate situation, even if export income is going up. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700514_reps_27_hor67/#subdebate-32-0)

* But if the Government was not afraid of losing <span class="highlight">votes</span> it would bc actual, it is hypothetical today because of that. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1970/19700514_reps_27_hor67/#subdebate-32-0)

* The honourable member for Reid claimed that during an election campaign in Western Australia I advised Country Party voters to give their second preference <span class="highlight">votes</span> to the Labor Party candidate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* Yet not so very long ago, in fact I think somewhat less than a year ago, those who are now in Opposition were sitting on the Government side of the House and opposing the proposition that 18-year-olds should have <span class="highlight">votes</span> just as vehemently as they are now sup porting it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* These people could see a threat to their position if 18-year-olds were in fact able to come forward and cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span> as to who should be governing this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* The Australian Labor Party is not concerned about the Territory because it is 2,000 or 3,000 miles from Melbourne and Sydney, or wherever the Labor members come from or get their <span class="highlight">votes</span> in the outer suburbs of the big cities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* Studies have shown that the first <span class="highlight">votes</span> of a young voter are more volatile, reflecting the fact that young people have not settled their political allegiances. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* And this applies also to the constituting city government throughout Australia; in some of our States most of the residents have no vote and some of the residents have 8 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* To bring the Country Party right up to date I state that at the 1972 elections the Country Party polled 9.44 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, won 20 seats and has 16 per cent voting strength in the House. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#debate-33)

* In 1961 the Labor Party polled 2,534,702 <span class="highlight">votes</span>, or 46.76 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, and in 1969 polled 2,870,792 or 46.95 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#debate-33)

* I turn to Queensland, this bastion of selected democracy where the Country Party reigns; where redistribution of boundaries has been the scorn of the Party since 1958; where it is possible for the Labor Party to gain 46.75 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, more than the combined <span class="highlight">votes</span> of the Liberal and Country parties (42.23 per cent) and to win only 33 seats as against 47 for the Government parties. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#debate-33)

* In that State the Country Party, with the lowest total vote - the lowest percentage of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> (20 per cent) - won 26 seats to the Liberal Party's 21 with 22.23 per cent of <span class="highlight">votes</span>, against 33 by Labor with 46.75 per cent of total <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#debate-33)

* The Country Party which polled a minority of <span class="highlight">votes</span>, and a minority of the percentage of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, holds the Premiership of the State of Queensland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730313_reps_28_hor82/#debate-33)

* It has real interest only in women's <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730314_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-28-0)

* My purpose in taking part in the debate has been simply to draw attention to the anomalies which are created in this legislation and which always are created when governments make decisions quickly without thinking out the consequences but simply to gain <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730314_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-28-0)

* We could have done it to gain <span class="highlight">votes</span> but we did not. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730314_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-28-0)

* Because of the understandable reaction of the  industry to the  imposition of the excise, members of the Labor Party saw the whole problem, from the beginning to this moment, purely in terms of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730314_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-29-0)

* But one of the difficulties which we should recognise in the Australian voting system for both Federal Houses is that it is the most complicated system of voting to be found in any country and it brings about the largest percentage of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, apparently, that one finds in any country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730315_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-8-0)

* Of course more than half the Aborigines are like that, but most of the people who cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span> for members of this House have scarcely ever seen the Aborigines at the other end of the spectrum - the people who are still living in tribal or near tribal conditions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730315_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-30-0)

* Indeed even in the reformed Australian Labor Party the trade union movement has some 60 per cent of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730327_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-45-0)

* Indeed, other members might be fearful that the image they project would at times not win them <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-16-0)

* Attributed to a former Labor Minister and  Senator was  the saying: 1 don't care who <span class="highlight">votes</span> or how they vote so long as I count them'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* If all divisions could be drawn so that their <span class="highlight">votes</span> were equal they would be greatly less than equal within months. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* These figures are derived as follows: 17 extra-metropolitan divisions in New South Wales, including Darling, cast 875,069 formal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* That is an average of 51,475 formal <span class="highlight">votes</span> per division, including Darling. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* Excluding that division's <span class="highlight">votes</span>, there were 834,369 formal <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in the other 16 divisions, giving an average of 52,148 <span class="highlight">votes</span> per division. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* Twenty-eight metropolitan divisions cast 1,531,877 formal <span class="highlight">votes</span> or 54,709 per division. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* In fact, in the last election the Labor Party polled fewer <span class="highlight">votes</span> in proportion than the percentage of seats it holds in this Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* He was never on record as criticising the property qualification of voting for the upper House or the system of local government in which most of the residents of Perth have no <span class="highlight">votes</span> and some have eight. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* What they stand by solidly is malapportionment to make sure that the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, at any rate of the Country Party segment, will always have a much greater value than those of anybody else. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* In the Westminster system where there will be monopoly of power for that side which has the majority of seats, there is a very clear moral obligation to ensure, so far as it is humanly possible, that the side which has the majority of seats has had the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* Its electoral system is identical with that of Melbourne, identical with that of Adelaide and identical with that of Perth in that most of the people have had no <span class="highlight">votes</span> and some have had a multiplicity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* It gives an equal weighting to the <span class="highlight">votes</span> of citizens. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* The Constitution does not provide for equal value of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* Equality of representation should be seen to be far more important than mere mathematical equality of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#debate-21)

* It received on occasions the majority of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in the nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* It is very interesting that in one of the areas in this State to which the Leader of the Country Party drew attention there is a mayor who sits with no fewer than 28 formal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* They want their <span class="highlight">votes</span> to be of equal value. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* According to the Government the amendments proposed by this Bill will mysteriously ensure that all <span class="highlight">votes</span> will have equal value. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* No distribution should permit a situation where a party or coalition which secures a majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> does not secure a majority of members of the House of Representatives. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* Only once since 1 949 has the party or group of parties with a majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> failed to win a majority of seats in the House of Representatives. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* In 1972, Labor polled less than 50 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> but won 53.6 per cent of the seats - not a bad record for a Party competing against what is claimed to be, in terms of the assertions and the allegations put forward by the Government in this debate, an 'unfair' Electoral Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* When did one Liberal Party member of this Parliament stand up and outline the situation in the Upper House of South Australia where a party able to obtain 35 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> is able to obtain 80 per cent of the seats? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* In other words the honourable member for Wimmera is supporting a proposition where every elector in his electorate has 2 <span class="highlight">votes</span> in this Parliament to the one vote of the honourable member for Diamond Valley. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The honourable member for Kalgoorlie  (Mr Collard)  will have 100 <span class="highlight">votes</span> in this place. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* It would be similar to the position in Queensland where the Liberal Party - which at least receives about 30 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> - cannot obtain more seats than the Country Party which has 19 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and has a Country Party Premier imposed on it by a rigged electoral system and  not  by the will of the people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The  Deputy  Leader of the Opposition, just before he sat down, made a claim that in every election except the 1954 election the party which has obtained the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> has won the election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* In 1961 the Australian Labor Party obtained a greater percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> than did the combined Government parties and their supporters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* Government parties obtained a greater number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> than did the Australian Labor Party in every election except the one in 1954. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The Communist Party gets so few <span class="highlight">votes</span> that it is the most insignificant party in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The Australia Party has received a significant number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> in elections it has contested and it has directed its preferences to the Australian Labor Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* If it is good enough for the Liberal Party to claim that DLP <span class="highlight">votes</span> are Liberal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, it is reasonable for us to claim that Australia Party <span class="highlight">votes</span> were <span class="highlight">votes</span> in support of a Labor government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The record of redistributions for Federal purposes has been free from charges of gerrymandering The fairness of recent redistributions has been demonstrated by election results where, in elections since 1949 with the exception of one - although one honourable member has challenged this - the Party or parties which gained the highest percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> throughout Australia formed the Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The results of the last election where Labor won 49.6 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and 53.6 per cent of the electorates would seem to underline the fairness of the 1968 redistribution. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* Any member of the Liberal Party who <span class="highlight">votes</span> for a gerrymander that favours the Country Party <span class="highlight">votes</span> against his interests, the interests of the Liberal Party and the interests of people who vote Liberal. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* The question of <span class="highlight">votes</span> for 18-year-olds was brought before the House quite separately. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730329_reps_28_hor82/#subdebate-25-0)

* In this debate we have pointed to a number of criteria, such as the overall result of the present electoral system, which is a majority of seats for the party which receives the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* Time and time again honourable members from this side of the House have said in this debate that since 1949 there has been only one election, that of 1954, in which the party which has achieved an overall majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> has not received an overall majority of seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* The point 1 am making is that when the Australian Labor Party got the <span class="highlight">votes</span> under the existing system in 1972 it got the numbers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* What it now wants to do is to so arrange things that it gets the numbers when it does not get the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* The statement by the honourable member for Barker  (Dr Forbes)  that only once since 1949 has the Party gaining the greatest number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> been unsuccessful in winning the most electorates, 1 believe, was an incorrect one because in 1961 and again in 1969 the <span class="highlight">votes</span> gained by the Australian Labor Party totalled more than the <span class="highlight">votes</span> gained by the parties now in Opposition. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* I do not subscribe - I make no apology for saying this - to a policy which gives country people up to 50 per cent advantage over city people in respect of the value of <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* In Queensland it took an average of 13,045 <span class="highlight">votes</span> to elect an ALP candidate and 6,972 to elect a Country Party candidate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* I can foresee, as  Mr Martin,  the  President  of the Young Liberals in Queensland, apparently had the foresight to realise, that if the Liberal Party wishes to sit idly by and allow the Country Party voting power to develop to such a degree that one vote in the country is worth 1 or 2 <span class="highlight">votes</span> in the city there certainly will be a reaction from people living in the cities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* But there are 10 senators from South Australia representing 350,000 people with <span class="highlight">votes</span> of the same value as 10 senators from New South Wales who represent 31 million people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* Those of us who sit on the Government side of the House - included in our ranks are more representatives of country electorates than any other political party has - say categorically that the value of all men's <span class="highlight">votes</span> should be equal, irrespective of where they live or what they do. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* With just over 8,000 primary <span class="highlight">votes</span>, he represents the people of McMillan - nearly 50,000 electors - in this House. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* Considering the views of the honourable member I am not surprised that he received only 8,000 odd <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* The views that he expressed in his maiden speech were the views of the League of Rights and it is surprising and deplorable to me that people with views such as those should receive even 8,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span> in any electorate in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-29-0)

* I think it needs to be noted - this is the ultimate test of fairness of an electoral system - that in the one year, under the first redistribution which we had undertaken, in which the Labor Party obtained a majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> in total that Party at the same time won office. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* In 1954 Labor won a greater number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> in total than did the present Opposition parties. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* But under all the redistributions that we have introduced the party that won the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> was the party that won office, and that includes the last election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* It will carry no weight with the Minister for Northern Development  (Dr Patterson)  and the Minister for Immigration  (Mr Grassby)  or at least with the people who elected them on the last occasion but will think better of it on the next, because they know that they have now elected to this Parliament a Government that is concerned only with <span class="highlight">votes</span> in large cities and is not concerned with the remoter country towns, provincial cities or the people who live in the rural communities - not just the farmers but the totality of people who live outside the great metropolitan areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* As a member for one of the larger electorates, I can fully appreciate the difficulties of distance in these large electorates and the amount of travel involved in endeavouring to give some service to the people, but I feel that this situation does not justify the large disparity in numbers that exists at present, lt should not be used to reduce the value of electors' <span class="highlight">votes</span> in other areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* But whilst we still have our anomalies in South Australia, I think we have lost our crown as the most gerrymandered State to Queensland, where we see the reins of government in the hands of a Party which is receiving only 20 per cent of the overall <span class="highlight">votes</span> of the Queensland people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730403_reps_28_hor83/#subdebate-32-0)

* And it was a successful frustration of the democratic process, for in the elections of 1950 the Liberal and Country Party team won a majority of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, actually 49.7 per cent, but gained only 31 of tha 75 seats, whereas Labor polled but 46.5 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> yet managed to get 42 of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* Obviously, the Government is trying to create a situation in which it would not need to get any more <span class="highlight">votes</span> to win more seats or, perhaps, the Government wants to win the same number of seats with many less <span class="highlight">votes</span> than it received on 2nd December. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* At present there is no doubt that, with one exception in the last 25 years or more, the Party which received the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> became the Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* The Government would have a redistribution and create a situation in which the Labor Party, with the same number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> that it received at the last election, would win a vastly increased majority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* No-one disagrees with the slogan of one man one vote, but what this really means is that in a democracy the government should be won by the party which obtains a majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* I could not help thinking that they must have coalesced some way and discussed it, because it was precisely the same speech that his father made here in days gone by, depending to the last drop on the right of the Country Party for special consideration because it cannot obtain <span class="highlight">votes</span> from the Australian people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* A few moments ago the honourable member for Farrer said that only once since 1949 has the party that obtained the majority of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> not won the election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* The facts are that in 1954 the Australian Labor Party won 50.1 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and gained 56 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* The LiberalCountry Party with 47 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> gained 58 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* In 1961 the Labor Party gained 46.76 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and won 62 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* In 1961 the Labor Party won 46.76 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and gained 62 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

* The Liberal-Country Party won 40.91 per sent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and gained the same number of seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1973/19730404_reps_28_hor83/#debate-32)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740306_reps_28_hor88/#debate-24)

* It is merely an attempt to gain a few miserable <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740306_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-25-0)

* It is no wonder that there is now a case before the Court of Disputed Returns on the question of Coogee where a Labor candidate was allegdly defeated by 8 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740307_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-42-0)

* If so, in view of the forthcoming Senate election, will he clarify the position 'for electors in order to avoid confusion and informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-17-0)

* In view of the projected legislation dealing with the registration of political parties and, just as importantly the forthcoming Senate election, it is necessary for the people to know precisely the parties contesting elections in order that they may avoid in many ways informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-17-0)

* So I ask the city dwellers to make sure that they vote for the National Party, and the country dwellers to make sure that they vote for the National Alliance because it is important that confusion does not force them to make what might be termed informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-17-0)

* So the people should be aware that when they vote for the National Alliance they vote for 2 parties and, in effect they have struck the jackpot - 2 <span class="highlight">votes</span> for one. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-17-0)

* I hope this explanation will avoid people casting a false vote and, in effect, will avoid people casting informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> at the forthcoming Senate election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-17-0)

* In the same year the United Australia Party-Country Party polled 44.26 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> yet won only 23 seats  -  2 per cent more than Labor polled but 12 fewer seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-41-0)

* In 1950 Labor won 46.3 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and 42 seats, the Liberal-Country Party 48 per cent or 2 per cent more than Labor but 31 seats  -  11 seats fewer than the Labor Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-41-0)

* Of course what they do not say is that that was the percentage of the total <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in all Queensland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-41-0)

* A very different result would be obtained if the Country Party vote were quoted as a percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> obtained in electorates where it fields candidates and then compared with the percentage that the Labor Party gains in seats where it fields candidates. * We have a situation in Western Australia, for instance, where in one Upper House electorate there are 85,000 electors and in another electorate there are 5,400 electors, a difference which represents an effective 15 <span class="highlight">votes</span> for an elector in one electorate compared with one vote for an elector in another electorate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740312_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-45-0)

* In South Australia at the moment - and this system is about to be abolished - there is an upper House in which the party that has 56 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> in the lower House can get only 4 to 6 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740313_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-18-0)

* In Western Australia the differential between the largest and the smallest seat in the upper House is 15 to one - a range of 85,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span> down to 5,000, and that is a greater differential than any democratic system can stand. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740313_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-18-0)

* After all, we are all elected to represent people and we have to represent people who do not have <span class="highlight">votes</span> because they are not yet 18 years of age; we. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740314_reps_28_hor88/#subdebate-12-0)

* The Australian Labor Party in that State won 5 seats with 46 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, and the Liberal party won 5 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* On 18 May last the Country Party polled 10.7 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* I mention the following matters in order to bring the situation up to date: In Queensland, for instance, the Australian Labor Party with 48 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>- more than the combined total of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> of all the other parties- holds only 33 seats; yet the combined parties with 42 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> hold 47 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In Queensland it takes 13,045 <span class="highlight">votes</span> to elect a Labor member, 9,600 <span class="highlight">votes</span> to elect a Liberal member and 6,972 <span class="highlight">votes</span> to elect a Country Party member. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* The answer to the problem of representing country seats is not to weight the electorates for country members but to give them adequate facilities to carry out their responsibilities and to reach their electors and not by making country <span class="highlight">votes</span> worth more than city <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* The situation is that in 1954, 1961, 1969 and 1972, the Australian Labor Party obtained more <span class="highlight">votes</span> than were obtained by the parties of those who sit opposite. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* That principle is to ensure that every electorate shall have approximately the same number of electors, so that the <span class="highlight">votes</span> of all electors shall be equal in value. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* As the Leader of the Opposition has effectively pointed out, the real test of equitable electoral legislation is that the party which receives the majority of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> should also receive the majority of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* At that time in respect of the House of Representatives the present Government polled 49.3 per cent of the formal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and received 5 1 .96 per cent of the seats in the new Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In fact when the vote is expressed as a ratio of the percentage of seats to the percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> the result slightly favours the Labor Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* The Opposition is on record in this Parliament as supporting the principle that all <span class="highlight">votes</span> should have equal value. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In fact of the total <span class="highlight">votes</span> polled, the Australian Labor Party polled about 250,000 more than the combined <span class="highlight">votes</span> of the Liberal Party, the Country Party and the Democratic Labor Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* Gladstone once said: 'Do our opponents believe in counting <span class="highlight">votes</span> or weighing them?' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* It is where one gets the weighing of <span class="highlight">votes</span> to suit a series of areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* There is absolutely no doubt that the Australian people want a system which gives equality of value of <span class="highlight">votes</span> for all voters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* So it was assumed that, consistent with the constitutional requirement, there would be equality of value of <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in elections for this Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* It has been argued in this Parliament in the past that there has never been an occasion when the party with the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> has not had the majority of seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In 1972 the Australian Labor Party gained 49.59 per cent of the primary <span class="highlight">votes</span> and 41.48 per cent of the primary <span class="highlight">votes</span> went to the Liberal and Country Parties. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* It took that proportion of the primary <span class="highlight">votes</span> to change the government and put the category A boys in their place. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* With one exception the party that got the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> formed the Government, and that is the real test. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* Are the people of Australia to trust government of the future to a Country Party that can poll at best, say, 10 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and demand 1 6 per cent of the seats? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* The justification for the Senate was the preservation of State rights, not the destruction of <span class="highlight">votes</span> for city people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* Admittedly, as a result of the double dissolution we did remove a splinter Party which supported the Liberal Party and the Australian Country Party through thick and thin but did not have enough <span class="highlight">votes</span> to have one person elected to the House of Representatives. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In the present situation, the Labor Party can poll 5 or 6 per cent or more of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> than the Opposition Parties but can only obtain a narrow majority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* The facts are that in 1972 the Australian Labor Party received 49.6 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and 53.6 per cent of the seats and won Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* It is a fact- the honourable members for Phillip  (Mr Riordan)  tried to ignore it but it is a simple fact- that the only redistribution that did not present the perfect result in terms of seats won for percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> won was the 1949 redistribution which was brought in by Labor itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* On that occasion the Labor Government tried to gerrymander the electorates and all the prima donnas wanted safe seats with a majority of about 20,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* After the South Australian elections in 1968, when the Labor Party received almost 54 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> but were defeated in government, 20,000 people marched from the parade grounds in Adelaide to Light Square to demonstrate against the iniquitous electoral system that operated in that State. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* In 9 elections held under  Sir Thomas  Playford 's Government, Labor won the majority of <span class="highlight">votes</span> in 8 elections but it never governed during that period. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* It needed only 11 more <span class="highlight">votes</span> in one seat in that State, as my friend the honourable member for Stirling  (Mr Viner)  can confirm, and it would have won 60 per cent of the seats on 46 per cent of the State vote. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* That principle is to ensure that every electorate shall have approximately the same number of electors, so that the <span class="highlight">votes</span> of all of the electors shall be equal in value. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-3-0)

* I suggest that the reason lies in the means by which the Government expects that it can influence the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, to give it control of the Senate, in the representation from those Territories. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* In 1970- the figures would be greater now, of course- a person required almost 300,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span> to be elected as a senator in New South Wales. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* In Victoria he required almost 225,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* But to be elected a senator for the Australian Capital Territory all that would have been required in 1973 was 28,000 <span class="highlight">votes</span> and to be elected a senator from the Northern Territory all that would have been required was 10,600 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* If one examines the Northern Territory and the Australian Capital Territory and considers the methods which have been adopted one can only believe that the intent of this Bill is to ensure that representation from both of those places ultimately will be secured for a Labor Government which, by the expenditure of money, buys <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* It is by this means that we have seen developing in this country the use of patronage in order to secure <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* That is patronage, that is corruption and that is the way in which <span class="highlight">votes</span> can be won and it was the way in which of course, prior to the English Reform Acts, <span class="highlight">votes</span> were won in the United Kingdom. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* In 1972 the Liberal Party secured 26 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and again the result would have been the same and members of the Labor Party know this. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* Nevertheless, I am confident, the belief of the Labor Party is that by the distribution of Government largesse and by the exercise of patronage the necessary <span class="highlight">votes</span> can be secured. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* It is a Bill which would give a disproportionate influence to the Territory senators so that they would have the deciding <span class="highlight">votes</span> in any issue on which, having regard to the equality of State representation, the major parties would be equally divided. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19740806_reps_29_hor89/#subdebate-4-0)

* These include: optional preferential marking of ballot-paper; printing of party affiliations of candidates on ballot-papers; registration of political parties for purposes of identification and printing of affiliations on ballot-papers; introduction of mobile polling booths at hospitals and similar institutions; drawing for positions of candidates on House of Representatives ballot-papers; closing of the polls at 6 p.m. rather than 8 p.m.; requiring a candidate changing his name within 12 months prior to nominations to declare the change, and providing for the former name to be included on the ballotpaper; prevention of persons enrolling or nominating for election under changed names in certain circumstances; an earlier deadline for the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and for the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> direct to respective returning officers; restricting postal vote application forms to be used at an election or referendum to those specified by notice in the Gazette; prohibiting the listing of names of persons who apply for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, except in certain specified circumstances; providing postal voting facilities for prisoners who have retained their franchise entitlements; increasing the amount of deposit required with nomination and varying the conditions under which deposits may be saved; preservation of the voting entitlement of Australian citizens posted overseas in the service of the Crown, and retention on the roll of the name of an elector temporarily absent from his address; precluding nomination for election to the Australian Parliament of a member of the Legislative Assembly of the Northern Territory or the Australian Capital Territory; prevention of a person from nominating as a candidate for more than one Federal election held on the same day; protection of candidates against the issue of misleading how-to-vote cards; change in qualifications for enrolment, voting and candidature from 'British subject' to 'status of a British subject'; eliminating the need to state the address of author in the case of broadcasting or telecasting of political matters; the manner of announcing the name of an author of political matter on radio or television; responsibility for publication of matter or comment of a political nature in the Press between issue of the writ and the close of the poll; removal of the restriction on exhibition of electoral posters within a hall or room being used for political party meetings; provision of support staff for Distribution Commissioners; authority for alterations to the roll when a street is renamed or renumbered; lowering the permissible age of presiding officers or assisting presiding officers to 18 years; appointment of substitute assistant returning officer at places outside Australia in certain circumstances; increases in penalties for failure to enrol; the provision of fines as an alternative to imprisonment where relevant; amounts of monetary penalties to match imprisonment terms; amendment of questions to be put to voters by presiding officers; conversion of distances to metric measurements; use of 'given names' in lieu of 'Christian names'; candidates making gifts, donations, etc., prior to an election; retitling of the Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19741125_reps_29_hor92/#subdebate-33-0)

* The proposal is to amend the Act so that the candidate retains his deposit if the total number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> polled in his favour as first preference <span class="highlight">votes</span> is more than 10 per cent of the total number of first preferences polled in the election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19741125_reps_29_hor92/#subdebate-33-0)

* On the basis that it has, my scheme aims to superimpose the entire preferential voting pattern of a candidate on to the vote of the elector who <span class="highlight">votes</span> for that candidate only. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19741125_reps_29_hor92/#subdebate-33-0)

* If a party, person or government seeks, by legal means, to deny a disadvantaged section of the community its voting rights this can be achieved by placing complications or difficulties in the way of voting which will prevent a substantial proportion of the population from casting formal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19741125_reps_29_hor92/#subdebate-33-0)

* In the last Senate election a deliberate nomination of candidates took place in New South Wales for the purpose of creating informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>- in your electorate,  Mr Speaker,  20 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast for the Senate were informalto the advantage of a political party which suffers least from the casting of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. * -I say that because the proportion of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in Labor seats was nearly double on average the proportion of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in Liberal seats, and the margin between 6 seats and 5 seats in New South Wales was only 4 per cent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1974/19741125_reps_29_hor92/#subdebate-33-0)

* -What I am saying-I think if you look at the statistics I will not need to say it too often- is that the order in which the seats rank in accordance with the percentage of Labor <span class="highlight">votes</span> almost exactly relates to the order in the number of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in the Senate election. * One can hardly expect the percentage of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> to be less than they were at the last election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The highest percentage of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> is 3.7 and the percentages range down to one point something. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The Government seeks to have electoral reform whereby citizens of Australia in casting their <span class="highlight">votes</span> will be able to do so with knowledge, with understanding, being able to identify clearly the persons who are offering themselves for election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* On a personal basis, the honourable member may get a few <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The most obvious exercise that has ever been undertaken to ensure that many candidates contest a ballot in order to bemuddle the people was undertaken, of course, during the Senate selection that was conducted together with the House of Representatives election following the double dissolution in 1974 in relation to which a political research team discovered that the Australian Labor Party would lose 80 per cent of the additional informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> for every candidate above the number of 40 who ran at that election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Elements such as the period of polling, the way in which postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> can be recorded, and the amount of deposits all form part of that system of fairness. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The document states that, if a great number of candidates can be nominated for Senate elections, this will cause so many informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> that certain parties could be defeated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* These people are working on the basis that in the very heavily industrialised seats represented by the Labor Party the proportion of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> would be the greatest, and the document goes on to prove this chapter and verse. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* When we consider that, amongst the 73 candidates, some received only 150 <span class="highlight">votes</span> out of about 2 million <span class="highlight">votes</span>, nobody could say that these were not frivolous candidates. * I do not think it would mitigate against any serious contender for political honours, and it certainly would stop those who nominate and get 23, 50 or 150 <span class="highlight">votes</span>, out of a couple of million, causing not only great inconvenience to some individuals but also great cost and at the same time a tremendous number of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Either they will have to alter the Senate system of voting to make it simpler so that the number of candidates will not matter in relation to the number of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, or they will have to face up to what is a reasonable amount for the deposit. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* In the first place, the Minister referred to the number of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* But if he were to examine the informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in the election we all have in mind- the Senate election for New South Wales in which there were 73 candidates- he would find that the informal percentage was not greatly different from the percentage in the election held in 1 96 1 . [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Either they thought the candidates were frivolous or they thought they were of insufficient weight; but, whatever the reasoning was, those candidates did not get many <span class="highlight">votes</span> as a percentage, and that is what matters in a Senate count under the proportional representation system that we use. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* That amendment is consequent on the decision that postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> must be returned to the respective divisional returning officers by the close of the poll. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* That proposition is put forward simply in connection with the motion which was moved elsewhere and is in line with the Opposition's view that in a condition of compulsory voting there should be no restriction on the facilities that are provided and that therefore the cut-off time at the end of the polling day- be it 8 o'clock or 6 o'clock ultimately- will represent the end of the receipt of <span class="highlight">votes</span> that can be included in the count. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* In relation to the return of the postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, under the postal voting system it is possible at this stage to vote after the close of the poll on the Saturday night. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* That is one reason why the postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> ought to be in the electoral office on the night of the poll. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* So this clause makes an attempt not to prevent people from voting but to see that all <span class="highlight">votes</span> are in on the night the election is held. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* In practically every country if the <span class="highlight">votes</span> are not in on the night of the poll they are not counted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* People know by half past 10 or 11 o'clock at night who has won the election because the <span class="highlight">votes</span> are in the box. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* There can be no doubt, as a result of the common form which has existed over the years, that people who consider themselves smart electioneers have been able to manipulate the manner in which they are able to get people to cast postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Conditions exist under which people are eligible for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Firstly, many people who cast postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> perhaps do not want to vote at all but are coerced into voting. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Secondly, many people who cast postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> are not eligible to do so because they do not comply with the laws set down on the postal vote form. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* By looking at the figures concerning postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> that were cast one can see how expert the political parties of Australia are becoming at going around hospitals, nursing homes and old folks' homes trying to make people vote when in fact they do not want to vote or they have an excuse for not voting. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* There is no doubt that the people involved- not just the political parties but all candidates- are becoming increasingly aware, particularly in the marginal electorates, of the importance of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* This is a patently very obvious method of doing away with their <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The one great characteristic of the Australian voting system, which has been denigrated, rubbished and criticised, is that it is the only voting system in the world which is designed to guarantee that nobody is elected unless he gets 50 per cent plus one of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* This proposed amendment has in it the ingredients to destroy the proposition that nobody can be elected in Australia unless they receive 50 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> plus one vote. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The Government is seeking to provide by this legislation that a person can be elected with less than 50 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* I can say only that the Minister for Services and Property, who has been good at getting <span class="highlight">votes</span> himself, has had this proposition put on him by someone else. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* So, I do not think in these provisions we ought to be concentrating on improving the percentage of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* He said that in Britain postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> have to be in by the close of the polls. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* What the Government would do by maintaining this provision would be to cut out a number of people who are at present able to register postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> either because of delays in mail, because of remoteness, or because a person was ill and put off voting for a few days. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* People in country areas ought to be assisted to cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span> for the candidates of their choice rather than prevented from doing it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* We know that even with the period that is provided now some <span class="highlight">votes</span> are received too late. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* It refers to those people in remote areas and to the difficulty that they have in getting postal vote application forms and ballot papers in time and in having them returned so that their <span class="highlight">votes</span> can be counted- in fact, so that these people can vote. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* What is suggested here is that the divisional returning officer for a division that exceeds 26 000 square kilometres shall keep a register to be called the 'Register of General Postal Voters', and such persons shall receive automatically application forms for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Presumably it is because they think that these <span class="highlight">votes</span> will not favour the Australian Labor Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* I take this opportunity to make a plea to anyone who might be listening in these remote areas to do their best to get these <span class="highlight">votes</span> in, even if it means considerable inconvenience in travelling to a booth because of the uncertainty of the mails. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Of course our complaint is that postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> come in long after the booths are closed and Australia and the rest of the world has to wait to see who is to govern this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Of course under the Opposition's proposal a returning officer on the night on which the poll closes could say: 'There is only 50 <span class="highlight">votes</span> difference between the sitting member and the candidate for the other major political party'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* He would immediately look at the postal voting register to see how many people he had not received <span class="highlight">votes</span> from and would have an immediate check on whom he could get in touch with to go out and see those persons to make sure that some son of postal vote was recorded on behalf of those people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Then he would make sure that there was some evidence that the <span class="highlight">votes</span> were posted before 6 p.m. or 8 p.m., whatever is the time specified in this Bill when it is finally passed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* We say that Australia has to wait far too long for the return of those postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> to get a decision for the country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Under section 89 (3) as it now stands, applications for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> are open for public inspection from and including the third day after polling day. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* That provision currently is used by political organisations and candidates to make lists of all postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> for use at later elections. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* It is proposed to prohibit the listing of names of persons who apply for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, except where the Divisional Returning Officer is satisfied that it is required in connection with a genuine inquiry into possible malpractice. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* It is the view of the Opposition that the clause is intended to prevent persons from inspecting lists of those people who have applied for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* Briefly, the reason for closing off this section is to prevent things happening such as that which the honourable member for Griffith  (Mr Donald Cameron)  admitted he was an expert in doing- the canvassing of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, the applications being freely available, the forms being available from year to year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* In effect he has been going very close to infringing the Act by canvassing and soliciting postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* You cannot solicit postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, tell people that they can get them and all this kind of thing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* That advertisement by the honourable member for Griffith about postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> goes terribly close to breaching the Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* One has only to look at the voting returns for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and the pattern of voting to be able to see that some extraneous influence is being brought to bear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* My scrutineers reported to me that the number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> coming in for the Liberal candidate from the first batches of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>- these were the first postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> put out and were ones that had been solicited- showed a pattern of voting much more in favour of the Liberal candidate than was the voting trend in any sub-division in the whole electorate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The point I am making is that these <span class="highlight">votes</span> were specially solicited. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* The situation is that in many electorates groups, belonging not only to the Liberal Party, have gone out to hospitals where sick people are and have organised the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* They know from an examination of the lists that these people are there and that their <span class="highlight">votes</span> can be solicited. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* As the honourable member for Griffith said, these people are stood over and their <span class="highlight">votes</span> are obtained. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* What we will never be able to do by legislation is to prevent candidates of any political party compiling special lists of names of people who are known to be infirm or ill whom they then canvass to solicit their <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-26)

* After all, the present Labor Government was elected at the last election on 49 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* The Opposition believes that if voting is to be compulsory electors should be given every opportunity to have their <span class="highlight">votes</span> counted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* Postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> are the only way by which many ill people, travellers or people living in remote areas can vote. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* The Government's proposals require postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> to be lodged no later than the close of the poll. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* This would replace the present 10-day delay from the close of poll to the counting of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* It would disfranchise those who did not submit their postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> several days before the poll. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* In Western Australia we have seen several things of note happen: Firstly, the rather unusual circumstances surrounding the appointment of the Western Australian commissioners; secondly, the results of the boundaries of a special redistribution in Western Australia in which the Government gained nearly 60 per cent of the seats on 44 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* It was only 12 <span class="highlight">votes</span> away from obtaining 60 per cent of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* Thirdly, in a count of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> for the seat of Stirling- which, as honourable members will be aware, ran to within a margin of 12 <span class="highlight">votes</span>- we saw a recount discovering that many <span class="highlight">votes</span> or one or two more in ballot papers which up to then had been counted a number of times. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* I was present at the table as one of the two scrutineers when those <span class="highlight">votes</span> were discovered. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* In one ballot box 1 1 1 <span class="highlight">votes</span> were found in one bundle that was supposed to contain 100 and 97 in the other that was supposed to contain 100. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* Since the original phoned in, figures were correct and those <span class="highlight">votes</span> counted in the divisional office were incorrect it was a stra'nge 'proceeding. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* I refer also to the refusal of the opportunity to scrutineer a recount of the Western Australian Senate <span class="highlight">votes</span> in spite of the fact that that count was carried over many days making it impracticable for any party to have it scrutineered- there were also many complaints from electoral officers that they were tired and working under difficult conditions- and in spite of the fact that a recount was allowed at an earlier Senate election for an objecting Australian Labor Party candidate, when the percentage difference was greater than was the case in the last Western Australian Senate election. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#subdebate-26-0)

* The whole purpose of preferential voting is to be absolutely certain that when all the preferences have been counted, when all the <span class="highlight">votes</span> have been counted, whoever wins can say that a majority of the people voted for him, either as a first preference or as a second preference. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750410_reps_29_hor94/#debate-28)

* In fact I cannot remember an occasion when there has been a unanimous point of view on associated Bills on the Opposition side and a similar point of view on the Government side, that the Bills have not been debated cognately although separate <span class="highlight">votes</span> have been taken on each Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#subdebate-32-0)

* It is a device to try to maximise Labor Party <span class="highlight">votes</span> in city areas at the expense of country people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#subdebate-32-0)

* The fact of the matter is that a redistribution is being carried out which will require an abnormal percentage of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> to put the present Government out of office. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#subdebate-32-0)

* This point is worth stressing, given the frequent assertions which have been made by Country Party spokesmen to the effect that the percentage of seats won by the Government and Opposition in recent elections has accurately reflected the number of <span class="highlight">votes</span> polled. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* For example, at the 1972 House of Representatives elections the Country Party polled 9.44 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, yet was able to win 16 per cent of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* In relation to charges about previous elections reflecting accurately the vote which was given to the various parties, it is suggested that because in 1974 the Labor Party received as a second preferred vote 51.7 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, that it is fair and equitable that we receive 52 per cent of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* The Liberal Party and the National Country Party which received 48.3 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> received 48 per cent of the seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* In 1963 the present Opposition which was then led by  Sir Robert  Menzies on a second preferred vote received 52.6 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and had a majority of 22 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* In 1972 on a second preferred vote we received 52.7 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> and had a majority of 9 seats. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* The Whitiam Government is trying to achieve an electoral system that will keep it in office, similar to the situation that now exists in the United Kingdom where the Labor Party is holding office with 39.5 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span>, with 6 1 per cent of the <span class="highlight">votes</span> against it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750521_reps_29_hor95/#debate-33)

* One can produce facts and figures to show that a national vote one way will equate with a number of seats for one party; that a national percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> one way will equate conversely with the other party in terms of seats.
