* Because the Senate amendments have the effect of removing from the Bill the electoral reforms agreed to by this House, in particular the major reforms contained in the clauses dealing with optional preferential voting for Senate and House of Representatives elections, the printing of party affiliations against the names of candidates on ballot papers for the purpose of clarifying the choice open to electors when they cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span>, the drawing for positions on ballot papers at House of Representatives elections, and those reforming postal voting procedures. * My colleague the honourable member for Bennelong  (Mr Howard)  and other colleagues took the opportunity, when debating boundaries recently, to point out that if they had been agreed to, the percentage of seats obtained by the Labor Party would be greater than the percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span> it would get. * We intend therefore by this Bill to assist the electors to knowingly record their <span class="highlight">votes</span>, particularly in circumstances where they are uncertain of, or unable to ascertain, the political affiliations of the candidates appearing on the ballot paper. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750828_reps_29_hor96/#subdebate-29-0)

* These faculties, together with the availability of modern day private and public transport, are adequate to enable electors to conveniently record their <span class="highlight">votes</span>, and effectively eliminates the need to keep the polling booths open until 8 p.m. A by-product of the earlier closing hour is that the scrutiny can commence 2 hours earlier with the result that the counting trend for which the nation is waiting is known much earlier in the night of polling day. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750828_reps_29_hor96/#subdebate-30-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750828_reps_29_hor96/#subdebate-31-0)

* This facility would be a significant step forward in making it easier for the aged and infirm to register their <span class="highlight">votes</span>, while at the same time removing the need for canvassers and political party organisers to invade the hospitals, convalescent homes and institutions, as they do at present. * This Bill, the last in the series of Bills incorporating proposals previously contained in the Electoral Laws Amendment BUI, provides for: A speedier finalisation of election results, by introducing an earlier deadline for the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and by providing for the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> direct to the respective returning officer; prohibition on the listing of names of persons who apply for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, except in certain specified circumstances; restriction of postal vote application forms to be used at an election or referendum to those specified by notice in the Australian Government Gazette; postal voting faculties for prisoners who have retained their franchise entitlements; discretion to appoint a licensed or registered surveyor as a Distribution Commissioner in lieu of the Surveyor-General of the State concerned; and other minor amendments to the existing electoral law. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19750828_reps_29_hor96/#subdebate-32-0)

* I can remember when I narrowly lost an election in 1969 because an extraordinary number of absentee <span class="highlight">votes</span> came in from a place called Werris Creek which everybody knows is a little railway town in the north-west of New South Wales, not known as a place to which people from Bondi go for their annual holidays. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* Nevertheless, these <span class="highlight">votes</span> all turned up and honourable members would be surprised at the way they went. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* The Minister for Housing and Construction  (Mr Riordan)  put up some argument about what happened in his electorate with absentee <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* We are not talking about absentee <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* We are speaking about postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* There is enough of this happening- that is to say people being unable to lodge valid <span class="highlight">votes</span>, to demonstrate the need for amendment to the law. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* The argument put on absentee <span class="highlight">votes</span> is invalid. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* After section 1 1 3 of the Principal Act the following section is inserted:- ' 1 13a ( 1) Where a hospital is a polling place, the presiding officer may make arrangements with an appropriate person, or appropriate persons, on the staff of the hospital for the <span class="highlight">votes</span> of patients in the hospital or in part of the hospital to be taken in accordance with this section. ' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* <span class="highlight">votes</span> may be taken under this section at a special polling place at such time or times as the presiding officer determines, being a time or times between 8 o'clock in the morning and 6 o'clock in the evening  on polling day or on one or more of the 5 days preceding polling day, and at no other time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#debate-22)

* We do not go to hospitals with 400, 500 or 600 beds because we are interested in getting all the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-0)

* Whilst the present system continues the candidates will have no alternative but to do their utmost to ensure that they maximise their opportunities for gaining <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-0)

* My scrutineers noticed at the last election that the postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> which were cast early, the ones that were organised in hospitals, for example, showed a much greater support for the Liberal Party than would be the case in any subdivision in the whole electorate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-0)

* Members of the Liberal Party or people paid by them had gone around the hospitals and organised the <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-0)

* I fail to believe that these <span class="highlight">votes</span> would be any different in normal circumstances from the <span class="highlight">votes</span> that would apply in the rest of the community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-0)

* The fact that it takes a bit longer to count and there is a little more inconvenience to officers of the Australian Electoral Office, who after all are paid to do the job, is really of small consequence against what is intended, which is to find the intention of the people as expressed through their <span class="highlight">votes</span> in the ballot box. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The Minister proposes to do 2 things in respect of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I talked about postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and particularly the needs of people in the remote regions a little earlier. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The Minister proposes to restrict the time within which postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> may be received. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* He is going to restrict a certain number of them, and their <span class="highlight">votes</span> are going to be invalid. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* That is the direct consequence of what is being done here, and I believe it is being done deliberately because the Government has come to the conclusion that by and large those postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> that come in late do not favour it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* -Therefore the more the Government can cut down these <span class="highlight">votes</span> the better. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I was pleased to hear agreement from the honourable member for Griffith  (Mr Donald Cameron)  because I know that he among many members here is very knowledgeable in the field of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I notice from looking at election results that he seems to find at the time these <span class="highlight">votes</span> are counted that he is very popular with the majority of people who vote in this manner. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Far more serious than that is clause 10 which provides that postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> need to be received by the divisional returning officer by the close of the poll; that is to say, 8 p.m. on polling day or, as the Government would like, 6 p.m. We oppose that change. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* That will have the effect of making invalid a significant number of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The present situation is that we have up to 10 days after polling day to get postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> in. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* But the Government does not want that; it wants to eliminate the effectiveness of as many postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> as it can. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Of course not a lot of election results depend on postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* When they do, surely to heaven the aim should be to provide as great an opportunity as possible for electors on a particular roll to express their view and to cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* It would be a large restriction and would cut out 10 days for those who have to vote through the mail to have their <span class="highlight">votes</span> recorded. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Firstly, there is the earlier closing off of applications but, secondly and more importantly, there is the earlier time by which <span class="highlight">votes</span> have to be received before they can be counted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Many <span class="highlight">votes</span> are now received after polling day and 3 weeks, which is the time between nomination day and polling day, is not very long. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I think that is just an argument that is brought forward because it is so hard to make arguments other than the real one, which is the desire to cut down the number of valid <span class="highlight">votes</span> which are being cast through the post. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The clause would mean that postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> would have be be delivered or posted direct to the relevant divisional returning officer. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Our primary interest must be that a large degree of convenience is afforded to the public and that the result is the proper interpretation of the valid <span class="highlight">votes</span> that are cast by people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* It is a hypocritical exercise to talk about people voting when the Opposition supports a method of voting that ensures that a large percentage of <span class="highlight">votes</span>, particularly country <span class="highlight">votes</span>, are rendered informal. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* It is nonsense to talk about the number of electoral booths if, when the people cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span>, the <span class="highlight">votes</span> are then rendered informal by a complicated system of numbering. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* It is just mouthing words to come into the chamber and to try to put across a case for giving people an entitlement to vote if something is not done about ensuring that the <span class="highlight">votes</span> that are cast are formal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Provision is made for those <span class="highlight">votes</span> to get back to the booth. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Section 96 of the Electoral Act deals specifically with scrutiny by a divisional returning officer of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> and the opening of them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I was a scrutineer with respect to <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast in his electorate at the last 2 elections. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Under the system which operated in 1974 and which still continues at present, 1302 postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> were cast in the electorate of Paterson. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Of those <span class="highlight">votes</span>, 61 per cent went to the successful candidate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The unsuccessful candidate received 36 per cent of those postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The interesting point is this: As scrutineers, we had to challenge a considerable number of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> that carried postmarks dated several days after the date on which the election was held. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* There is no way in which the date when those <span class="highlight">votes</span> were cast can be determined. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I do not believe that all of those <span class="highlight">votes</span> were cast prior to 8 p.m. on 18 May 1974. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* A number of those <span class="highlight">votes</span> were challenged. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* We asked that a number of such postal <span class="highlight">votes</span> be passed on to the Electoral Officer for further investigation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* Looking at the result in the Paterson division in 1974, we find that the majority was 275 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* If we examine the difference between the percentages of <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast for each candidate at polling booths and the percentages of <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast for each candidate through the postal voting system, we find that the margin is sufficient to represent the difference between winning and losing that seat. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The net margin was 275 <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* So 53 500 people in the electorate of Paterson voted for one candidate or another and, in a final majority of 275 <span class="highlight">votes</span>, 140 people by the postal voting method selected the successful candidate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* When we look at the results in the 1972 election, we find that a similar situation emerges with respect to that abuse, as revealed by a comparison of the percentages of polling booth <span class="highlight">votes</span> and postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* The Opposition will not tell us that, as it knows that the present situation ensures that in country electorates a large proportion of voters cast informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> for Senate elections. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* They are dragged along to polling booths or make application for postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>, worrying about penalties for failing to vote, and cast their <span class="highlight">votes</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* All the time, honourable members opposite know full well in their own minds that they are wholeheartedly supporting a method of vote counting that ensures that the informal rate in <span class="highlight">votes</span> cast by country electors is almost twice the rate of informal <span class="highlight">votes</span> lodged by city electors. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751015_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-22-1)

* I would like to turn to a less emotional aspect of the Bill and refer to the endeavours by the Government to change the postal voting procedure by altering the deadline for the return of postal <span class="highlight">votes</span>. * The truth is of course that at the last Senate election the people not only recorded 200 000 more <span class="highlight">votes</span> for the Australian Labor Party candidates- the Government- than for all other Parties represented in the Senate combined, but elected 29 Labor senators and 29 Opposition senators and 2 Independents. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751021_reps_29_hor97/#debate-32)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751022_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-36-0)

* The Opposition will shortly face 7 million consumers and it will have to explain to those 7 million consumers, whose <span class="highlight">votes</span> they will be seeking, why it was that in the very area that concerns the consumers most of all- protection from dishonest advertising and protection from dishonest manufacturers, retailers and wholesalers- it has used this device to prevent an Act being put on the statute book. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/hofreps/1975/19751022_reps_29_hor97/#subdebate-41-0)
